					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Palestinian city in the West Bank</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the city in Palestine. print{.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:none!important}}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Palestine" <p><b>Jericho</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/ɛr/: &#39;err&#39; in &#39;merry&#39;">ɛr</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">JERR</span>-ik-oh</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">أريحا</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">Arīḥā</i></span>, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">IPA:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="ar-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic" title="Help:IPA/Arabic">&#91;ʔaˈriːħaː&#93;</a></span> <span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="ext-phonos-PhonosButton noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/f\/f4\/ArJericho.ogg\/ArJericho.ogg.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;ArJericho.ogg&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/ArJericho.ogg/ArJericho.ogg.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:ArJericho.ogg" title="File:ArJericho.ogg">ⓘ</a></sup></span>; <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <span lang="he" dir="rtl">יְרִיחוֹ</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Hebrew" title="Romanization of Hebrew">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><span title="Hebrew-language romanization"><i lang="he-Latn">Yərīḥō</i></span>) is a city in the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>; it is the administrative seat of the <a href="/wiki/Jericho_Governorate" title="Jericho Governorate">Jericho Governorate</a> of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Jericho is located in the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Valley" title="Jordan Valley">Jordan Valley</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_River" title="Jordan River">Jordan River</a> to the east and <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> to the west. In 2017, it had a population of 20,907.<sup id="cite_ref-PrelimCensus2017_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrelimCensus2017-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From the end of the era of <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a>, the city was <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian annexation of the West Bank">annexed and ruled by Jordan</a> from 1949 to 1967 and, with the rest of the West Bank, has been subject to <a href="/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Israeli occupation of the West Bank">Israeli occupation</a> since 1967; administrative control was handed over to the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Jericho is among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_continuously_inhabited_cities" title="List of oldest continuously inhabited cities">oldest cities in the world</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gates2003_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gates2003-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Murphyp288_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphyp288-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Freedmanp689_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedmanp689-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and it is also the city with the oldest known <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">defensive wall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Strutin_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strutin-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">Archaeologists</a> have unearthed the remains of more than 20 successive settlements in Jericho, the first of which dates back 11,000 years (to 9000&#160;BCE),<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> almost to the very beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a> epoch of the Earth's history.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Copious springs in and around the city have attracted human habitation for thousands of years.<sup id="cite_ref-Bromileyp715_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bromileyp715-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Jericho is described in the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> as the "city of palm trees".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, the archaeological site in the center of the city, known as <a href="/wiki/Tell_es-Sultan" title="Tell es-Sultan">Tell es-Sultan / Old Jericho</a>, was inscribed in <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s list as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in the State of Palestine, and described as the "oldest fortified city in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology">Etymology</h2></div>
<p>Jericho's name in <a href="/wiki/Modern_Hebrew" title="Modern Hebrew">Modern Hebrew</a>, <span title="Hebrew-language romanization"><i lang="he-Latn">Yeriẖo</i></span>, is generally thought to derive from the <a href="/wiki/Canaanite_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Canaanite language">Canaanite</a> word <i>rēḥ</i> <span class="gloss-quot">'</span><span class="gloss-text">fragrant</span><span class="gloss-quot">'</span>, but other theories hold that it originates in the Canaanite word <i>Yaraḥ</i> <span class="gloss-quot">'</span><span class="gloss-text"><a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">moon</a></span><span class="gloss-quot">'</span> or the name of the lunar deity <a href="/wiki/Yarikh" title="Yarikh">Yarikh</a>, for whom the city was an early centre of worship.<sup id="cite_ref-Schreiberp141_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schreiberp141-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Jericho's Arabic name, <span title="DIN 31635 Arabic (Arabic language) transliteration"><i lang="ar-Latn">Arīḥā</i></span>, means <span class="gloss-quot">'</span><span class="gloss-text">fragrant</span><span class="gloss-quot">'</span> and also has its roots in Canaanite <i>Reaẖ</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bromileyp1136_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bromileyp1136-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History_and_archaeology">History and archaeology</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Levantine_archaeology" title="Levantine archaeology">Levantine archaeology</a></div>
<p>The first excavations of the site were made by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Warren" title="Charles Warren">Charles Warren</a> in 1868. <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Sellin" title="Ernst Sellin">Ernst Sellin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Watzinger" title="Carl Watzinger">Carl Watzinger</a> excavated Tell es-Sultan and Tulul Abu el-'Alayiq between 1907 and 1909, and in 1911, and <a href="/wiki/John_Garstang" title="John Garstang">John Garstang</a> excavated between 1930 and 1936. Extensive investigations using more modern techniques were made by <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Kenyon" title="Kathleen Kenyon">Kathleen Kenyon</a> between 1952 and 1958. <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Nigro" title="Lorenzo Nigro">Lorenzo Nigro</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicol%C3%B2_Marchetti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nicolò Marchetti (page does not exist)">Nicolò Marchetti</a> conducted excavations in 1997–2000. Since 2009 the Italian-Palestinian archaeological project of excavation and restoration was resumed by Rome "<a href="/wiki/La_Sapienza" class="mw-redirect" title="La Sapienza">La Sapienza</a>" University and Palestinian MOTA-DACH under the direction of Lorenzo Nigro and Hamdan Taha, and Jehad Yasine since 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-sapienza_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sapienza-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Italian-Palestinian Expedition carried out 13 seasons in 20 years (1997–2017), with some major discoveries, like Tower A1 in the Middle Bronze Age southern Lower Town and Palace G on the eastern flanks of the Spring Hill overlooking the Spring of 'Ain es-Sultan dating from Early Bronze III.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Stone_Age:_Tell_es-Sultan_and_spring">Stone Age: Tell es-Sultan and spring</h3></div>
<p>The earliest excavated settlement was located at the present-day <a href="/wiki/Tell_es-Sultan" title="Tell es-Sultan">Tell es-Sultan</a> (or Sultan's Hill), a couple of kilometers from the current city. In both <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> and Hebrew, <i><a href="/wiki/Tell_(archaeology)" title="Tell (archaeology)">tell</a></i> means "mound" – consecutive layers of habitation built up a mound over time, as is common for ancient settlements in the Middle East and <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>. Jericho is the <a href="/wiki/Type_site" title="Type site">type site</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_A" title="Pre-Pottery Neolithic A">Pre-Pottery Neolithic A</a> (PPNA) and <a href="/wiki/Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_B" title="Pre-Pottery Neolithic B">Pre-Pottery Neolithic B</a> (PPNB) periods.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Natufian_hunter-gatherers,_c._10,000_BCE"><span id="Natufian_hunter-gatherers.2C_c._10.2C000_BCE"></span>Natufian hunter-gatherers, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 10,000 BCE</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Calibrated_Carbon_14_dates_for_Jericho_as_of_2013.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Calibrated_Carbon_14_dates_for_Jericho_as_of_2013.jpg/220px-Calibrated_Carbon_14_dates_for_Jericho_as_of_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="72" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Calibrated_Carbon_14_dates_for_Jericho_as_of_2013.jpg/330px-Calibrated_Carbon_14_dates_for_Jericho_as_of_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Calibrated_Carbon_14_dates_for_Jericho_as_of_2013.jpg/440px-Calibrated_Carbon_14_dates_for_Jericho_as_of_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="203" /></a><figcaption>Calibrated carbon 14 dates for Jericho as of 2013<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Reconstruction_of_the_Natufian-Jericho_skull.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Reconstruction_of_the_Natufian-Jericho_skull.jpg/220px-Reconstruction_of_the_Natufian-Jericho_skull.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Reconstruction_of_the_Natufian-Jericho_skull.jpg/330px-Reconstruction_of_the_Natufian-Jericho_skull.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Reconstruction_of_the_Natufian-Jericho_skull.jpg/440px-Reconstruction_of_the_Natufian-Jericho_skull.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="630" /></a><figcaption>Reconstruction of the Natufian-Jericho skull<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Epipaleolithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Epipaleolithic">Epipaleolithic</a> construction at the site appears to predate the invention of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, with the construction of <a href="/wiki/Natufian_culture" title="Natufian culture">Natufian culture</a> structures beginning earlier than 9000&#160;BCE, the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a> epoch in geologic history.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedmanp689_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedmanp689-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Jericho has evidence of settlement dating back to 10,000&#160;BCE. During the <a href="/wiki/Younger_Dryas" title="Younger Dryas">Younger Dryas</a> period of cold and drought, permanent habitation of any one location was impossible. However, the <a href="/wiki/Ein_as-Sultan_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Ein as-Sultan camp">Ein es-Sultan</a> spring at what would become Jericho was a popular camping ground for <a href="/wiki/Natufian" class="mw-redirect" title="Natufian">Natufian</a> hunter-gatherer groups, who left a scattering of crescent-shaped microlith tools behind them.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Around 9600&#160;BCE, the droughts and cold of the Younger Dryas <a href="/wiki/Stadial" class="mw-redirect" title="Stadial">stadial</a> had come to an end, making it possible for Natufian groups to extend the duration of their stay, eventually leading to year-round habitation and permanent settlement.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Pre-Pottery_Neolithic,_c._9500–6500_BCE"><span id="Pre-Pottery_Neolithic.2C_c._9500.E2.80.936500_BCE"></span>Pre-Pottery Neolithic, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 9500–6500 BCE</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tell_es-Sultan" title="Tell es-Sultan">Tell es-Sultan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_Jericho" title="Tower of Jericho">Tower of Jericho</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerycho8.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Jerycho8.jpg/220px-Jerycho8.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Jerycho8.jpg/330px-Jerycho8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Jerycho8.jpg/440px-Jerycho8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a><figcaption>Dwelling foundations unearthed at <a href="/wiki/Tell_es-Sultan" title="Tell es-Sultan">Tell es-Sultan</a> in Jericho</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Pre-Pottery Neolithic at Jericho is divided in Pre-Pottery Neolithic A and Pre-Pottery Neolithic B.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_A_(PPNA)"><span id="Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_A_.28PPNA.29"></span>Pre-Pottery Neolithic A (PPNA)</h5></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1251242444">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Jericho" title="Special:EditPage/Jericho">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The first permanent settlement on the site of Jericho developed near the Ein es-Sultan spring between 9,500 and 9000&#160;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As the world warmed up, a new culture based on agriculture and sedentary dwelling emerged, which archaeologists have termed "<a href="/wiki/Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_A" title="Pre-Pottery Neolithic A">Pre-Pottery Neolithic A</a>" (abbreviated as PPNA). Its cultures lacked pottery, but featured the following:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li>small circular dwellings</li>
<li>burial of the dead under the floor of buildings</li>
<li>reliance on hunting of wild game</li>
<li>cultivation of wild or domestic cereals</li></ul>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jericho_Statue.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Jericho_Statue.png/220px-Jericho_Statue.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="313" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Jericho_Statue.png 1.5x" data-file-width="272" data-file-height="387" /></a><figcaption>Head of an ancestor statue, Jericho, from c. 9000 years ago, among the oldest representations of a human face ever found. <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Archeological_Museum" title="Rockefeller Archeological Museum">Rockefeller Archeological Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>At Jericho, circular dwellings were built of <a href="/wiki/Adobe" title="Adobe">clay and straw</a> bricks left to dry in the sun, which were plastered together with a mud mortar. Each house measured about 5 metres (16&#160;ft) across, and was roofed with mud-smeared brush. Hearths were located within and outside the homes.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ziko.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Ziko.jpg/170px-Ziko.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Ziko.jpg/255px-Ziko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Ziko.jpg/340px-Ziko.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2373" data-file-height="3182" /></a><figcaption>The 8000 BCE <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_Jericho" title="Tower of Jericho">Tower of Jericho</a> at Tell es-Sultan</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Pre-Sultan (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;8350</span> – 7370&#160;BCE)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (February 2016)">dubious</span></a>&#32;&#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Jericho#Contradicts_dates_given_in_this_paragraph:_&quot;between_9,400_and_9000&quot;,_&quot;about_9400_BCE&quot;,_but_fits_somewhat_with_time_when_the_tower_was_used_according_to_Barkai_&amp;_Liran:_&quot;The_tower_was_constructed_and_used_between_≈8300_BCE_and_≈7800_BCE_(Burleigh_1981,_1983).&quot;_It_also_fits_with_starting_date_of_PPNB_indicated_in_the_next_paragraph." title="Talk:Jericho">discuss</a></i>&#93;</sup> is sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Neolithic#Fertile_Crescent" title="Neolithic">Sultanian</a>. The site is a 40,000 square metres (430,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) settlement surrounded by a massive stone wall over 3.6 metres (12&#160;ft) high and 1.8 metres (5&#160;ft 11&#160;in) wide at the base, inside of which stood a stone tower, over 8.5 metres (28&#160;ft) high, containing an internal staircase with 22 stone steps<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and placed in the centre of the west side of the tell.<sup id="cite_ref-BarkaiLiran_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BarkaiLiran-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This tower and the even older ones excavated at <a href="/wiki/Tell_Qaramel" title="Tell Qaramel">Tell Qaramel</a> in Syria<sup id="cite_ref-PaP2007_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PaP2007-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PCMA_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCMA-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are the oldest towers ever to be discovered. The wall of Jericho may have served as a defence against flood-water, with the tower used for ceremonial purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-PMMA57_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PMMA57-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The wall and tower were built during the Pre-Pottery Neolithic A (PPNA) period around 8000&#160;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-BarkaiJP_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BarkaiJP-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kenyon1981_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyon1981-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For the tower, carbon dates published in 1981 and 1983 indicate that it was built around 8300&#160;BCE and stayed in use until <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;7800&#160;BCE</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-BarkaiLiran_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BarkaiLiran-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The wall and tower would have taken a hundred men more than a hundred days to construct, thus suggesting some kind of social organization.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The town contained round mud-brick houses, yet no street planning.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The identity and number of the inhabitants of Jericho during the PPNA period is still under debate, with estimates going as high as 2,000–3,000, and as low as 200–300.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PMMA57_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PMMA57-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is known that this population had domesticated <a href="/wiki/Emmer_wheat" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmer wheat">emmer wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulse_(legume)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulse (legume)">pulses</a> and hunted wild animals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_B_(PPNB)"><span id="Pre-Pottery_Neolithic_B_.28PPNB.29"></span>Pre-Pottery Neolithic B (PPNB)</h5></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1251242444"><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Jericho" title="Special:EditPage/Jericho">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Pre-Pottery Neolithic B (PPNB) was a period of about 1.4 millennia, from 7220 to 5850&#160;BCE<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="Leaves two substantial gaps, one -, one +: if PPNB covers 9,500-9000, and PPN altogether ends around 6500, that leaves 1780 years belonging nowhere (9000-7220), and extends PPN from the stated 6500 by 650 years to 5850 BC. Must be addressed. (October 2021)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> (though <a href="/wiki/Carbon-14" title="Carbon-14">carbon-14</a>-dates are few and early). The following are PPNB cultural features:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Expanded range of domesticated plants</li>
<li>Possible <a href="/wiki/Domestic_sheep" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic sheep">domestication of sheep</a></li>
<li>Apparent <a href="/wiki/Cult_(religion)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cult (religion)">cult</a> involving the preservation of human skulls, with facial features reconstructed using <a href="/wiki/Plaster" title="Plaster">plaster</a>, and eyes set with shells in some cases</li></ul>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fertile_crescent_Neolithic_B_circa_7500_BC.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Fertile_crescent_Neolithic_B_circa_7500_BC.jpg/300px-Fertile_crescent_Neolithic_B_circa_7500_BC.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="311" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Fertile_crescent_Neolithic_B_circa_7500_BC.jpg/450px-Fertile_crescent_Neolithic_B_circa_7500_BC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Fertile_crescent_Neolithic_B_circa_7500_BC.jpg/600px-Fertile_crescent_Neolithic_B_circa_7500_BC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1050" data-file-height="1087" /></a><figcaption>Area of the <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;7500 BC</span>, with main sites. Jericho was a foremost site of the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Pottery_Neolithic" title="Pre-Pottery Neolithic">Pre-Pottery Neolithic</a> period. The area of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> proper was not yet settled by humans.</figcaption></figure>
<p>After a few centuries, the first settlement was abandoned. After the PPNA settlement phase, there was a settlement hiatus of several centuries, then the PPNB settlement was founded on the eroded surface of the <a href="/wiki/Tell_(archaeology)" title="Tell (archaeology)">tell</a>. This second settlement, established in 6800&#160;BCE, perhaps represents the work of an invading people who absorbed the original inhabitants into their dominant culture. Artifacts dating from this period include ten <a href="/wiki/Plastered_human_skulls" title="Plastered human skulls">plastered human skulls</a>, painted so as to reconstitute the individuals' features.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These represent either <a href="/wiki/Teraphim" title="Teraphim">teraphim</a> or the first example of <a href="/wiki/Portrait" title="Portrait">portraiture</a> in <a href="/wiki/Art_history" title="Art history">art history</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="see Tell Awad and discussion on Jericho&#39;s talk page (August 2013)">dubious</span></a>&#32;&#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Jericho#Dubious" title="Talk:Jericho">discuss</a></i>&#93;</sup> and it is thought that they were kept in people's homes while the bodies were buried.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedmanp689_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedmanp689-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Janson_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janson-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The architecture consisted of rectilinear buildings made of mudbricks on stone foundations. The mudbricks were loaf-shaped with deep thumb prints to facilitate bonding. No building has been excavated in its entirety. Normally, several rooms cluster around a central courtyard. There is one big room (6.5&#160;m ×&#160;4&#160;m (21.3&#160;<a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a> ×&#160;13.1&#160;ft)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="conversion via template displays unwarranted (false) precision (February 2018)">dubious</span></a>&#32;&#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Jericho#Dubious" title="Talk:Jericho">discuss</a></i>&#93;</sup> and 7&#160;m ×&#160;3&#160;m (23.0&#160;<a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a> ×&#160;9.8&#160;ft))<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="conversion via template displays unwarranted (false) precision (February 2018)">dubious</span></a>&#32;&#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Jericho#Dubious" title="Talk:Jericho">discuss</a></i>&#93;</sup> with internal divisions; the rest are small, presumably used for storage. The rooms have red or pinkish <a href="/wiki/Terrazzo" title="Terrazzo">terrazzo</a>-floors made of lime. Some impressions of mats made of reeds or rushes have been preserved. The courtyards have clay floors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Kathleen Kenyon interpreted one building as a <a href="/wiki/Shrine" title="Shrine">shrine</a>. It contained a niche in the wall. A chipped pillar of volcanic stone that was found nearby might have fitted into this niche.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The dead were buried under the floors or in the rubble fill of abandoned buildings. There are several collective burials. Not all the skeletons are completely articulated, which may point to a time of exposure before burial. A <a href="/wiki/Human_skull" class="mw-redirect" title="Human skull">skull</a> cache contained seven skulls. The jaws were removed and the faces covered with plaster; <a href="/wiki/Cowry" class="mw-redirect" title="Cowry">cowries</a> were used as eyes. A total of ten skulls were found. Modelled skulls were found in <a href="/wiki/Tell_Ramad" title="Tell Ramad">Tell Ramad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beisamoun" class="mw-redirect" title="Beisamoun">Beisamoun</a> as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Other finds included flints, such as arrowheads (tanged or side-notched), finely denticulated sickle-blades, <a href="/wiki/Burin_(lithic_flake)" title="Burin (lithic flake)">burins</a>, scrapers, a few <a href="/wiki/Tranchet_axe" title="Tranchet axe">tranchet axes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obsidian" title="Obsidian">obsidian</a>, and green obsidian from an unknown source. There were also <a href="/wiki/Quern-stone" title="Quern-stone">querns</a>, hammerstones, and a few ground-stone axes made of greenstone. Other items discovered included dishes and bowls carved from soft limestone, spindle whorls made of stone and possible loom weights, spatulae and drills, stylised anthropomorphic plaster figures, almost life-size, <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">anthropomorphic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theriomorphism" class="mw-redirect" title="Theriomorphism">theriomorphic</a> clay figurines, as well as shell and malachite beads.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 4th millennium BCE, Jericho was occupied during Neolithic 2<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (February 2016)">dubious</span></a>&#32;&#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Jericho#Neol._2_seems_to_be_equivalent_with_PPNB,_which_ends_long_before_M4_BCE._Unless_pottery_appeared_at_Jericho_later_than_M4,_this_is_a_mistake_AND_THIS_BELONGS_EITHER_UNDER_CHALCOLITHIC_OR_BRONZE_AGE." title="Talk:Jericho">discuss</a></i>&#93;</sup> and the general character of the remains on the site link it culturally with Neolithic 2 (or PPNB) sites in the West Syrian and Middle Euphrates groups. This link is established by the presence of rectilinear mud-brick buildings and plaster floors that are characteristic of the age.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Chalcolithic">Chalcolithic</h3></div>
<p>A succession of settlements followed from 4500&#160;BCE onward.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_Bronze_Age">Early Bronze Age</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_terracotta_Ancient_Bronze_period_3500-2000_BC_Tell_es-Sultan,_ancient_Jericho,_Tomb_A_IV,_Louvre_Museum_AO_15611.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Red_terracotta_Ancient_Bronze_period_3500-2000_BC_Tell_es-Sultan%2C_ancient_Jericho%2C_Tomb_A_IV%2C_Louvre_Museum_AO_15611.jpg/170px-Red_terracotta_Ancient_Bronze_period_3500-2000_BC_Tell_es-Sultan%2C_ancient_Jericho%2C_Tomb_A_IV%2C_Louvre_Museum_AO_15611.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Red_terracotta_Ancient_Bronze_period_3500-2000_BC_Tell_es-Sultan%2C_ancient_Jericho%2C_Tomb_A_IV%2C_Louvre_Museum_AO_15611.jpg/255px-Red_terracotta_Ancient_Bronze_period_3500-2000_BC_Tell_es-Sultan%2C_ancient_Jericho%2C_Tomb_A_IV%2C_Louvre_Museum_AO_15611.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Red_terracotta_Ancient_Bronze_period_3500-2000_BC_Tell_es-Sultan%2C_ancient_Jericho%2C_Tomb_A_IV%2C_Louvre_Museum_AO_15611.jpg/340px-Red_terracotta_Ancient_Bronze_period_3500-2000_BC_Tell_es-Sultan%2C_ancient_Jericho%2C_Tomb_A_IV%2C_Louvre_Museum_AO_15611.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1771" data-file-height="2492" /></a><figcaption>Red terracotta jar, Ancient Bronze period 3500–2000 BCE, Tell es-Sultan, ancient Jericho, Tomb A IV. <a href="/wiki/Louvre_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Louvre Museum">Louvre Museum</a> AO 15611.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In Early Bronze I, the strategraphic layers are Sultan IIIA1 (EB IA, c. 3500-3200 BCE) and Sultan IIIA2 (EB IB, c. 3200-3000 BCE).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In Early Bronze II, the strategraphic layers are Sultan IIIB1 (EB IIA, c. 3000-2850 BCE) and Sultan IIIB2 (EB IIB, c. 2850-2700 BCE).<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the Early Bronze IIIA (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2700</span> – 2500/2450&#160;BCE; Sultan IIIC1), the settlement reached its largest extent around 2600&#160;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>During Early Bronze IIIB (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2500</span>/2450–2350&#160;BCE; Sultan IIIC2) there was a Palace G on Spring Hill and city walls.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In Early Bronze IV, the strategraphic layers are Sultan IIID1 (EB IVA; 2300-2200 BCE) and Sultan IIID2 (EB IVB; 2200-2000 BCE).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Middle_Bronze_Age">Middle Bronze Age</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the Biblical battle, see <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jericho" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Jericho">Battle of Jericho</a>.</div>
<p>Jericho was continually occupied into the Middle <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age#Near_East" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>; it was destroyed in the Late Bronze Age, after which it no longer served as an urban centre. The city was surrounded by extensive defensive walls strengthened with rectangular towers, and possessed an extensive cemetery with vertical shaft-tombs and underground burial chambers; the elaborate funeral offerings in some of these may reflect the emergence of local kings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuijt2012167_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuijt2012167-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>During the Middle Bronze Age, Jericho was a small prominent city of the <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a> region, reaching its greatest Bronze Age extent in the period from 1700 to 1550&#160;BCE. It seems to have reflected the greater urbanization in the area at that time, and has been linked to the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Maryannu" title="Maryannu">Maryannu</a>, a class of chariot-using aristocrats linked to the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Mitanni" title="Mitanni">Mitannite</a> state to the north. Kathleen Kenyon reported "the Middle Bronze Age is perhaps the most prosperous in the whole history of Kna'an. ... The defenses ... belong to a fairly advanced date in that period" and there was "a massive stone <a href="/wiki/Revetment" title="Revetment">revetment</a> ... part of a complex system" of defenses.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Bronze Age Jericho fell in the 16th century at the end of the Middle Bronze Age, the calibrated carbon remains from its City-IV <a href="/wiki/Destruction_layer" title="Destruction layer">destruction layer</a> dating to 1617–1530&#160;BCE. Carbon dating <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1573&#160;BCE confirmed the accuracy of the stratigraphical dating <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1550.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Chronology (Nigro 2016)
</p>
<ul><li>Middle Bronze IA, Tell es-Sultan IVa1 (c. 2000/1950-1900 BC)</li>
<li>Middle Bronze IB, Tell es-Sultan IVa2 (c. 1900-1800 BC)</li>
<li>Middle Bronze IIA, Tell es-Sultan IVb1 (c. 1800-1700 BC)</li>
<li>Middle Bronze IIB, Tell es-Sultan IVb2 (c. 1700-1650 BC)</li>
<li>Middle Bronze IIC/III, Tell es-Sultan IVc (c. 1650-1550 BC)</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Late_Bronze_Age">Late Bronze Age</h3></div>
<p>There was evidence of a small settlement in the Late Bronze Age (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1400s BCE) on the site, but erosion and destruction from previous excavations have erased significant parts of this layer.<sup id="cite_ref-Davis_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Hebrew Bible narrative</dt></dl>
<p>The Hebrew Bible tells the story of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jericho" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Jericho">Battle of Jericho</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Joshua" title="Joshua">Joshua</a>, leading to the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaanite</a> city, the first one captured by the <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Promised_Land" title="Promised Land">Promised Land</a>. Archaeological excavations have failed to find traces of a fortified city at the site during the relevant time, the 13th century BCE at the end of the Bronze Age.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller1986_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller1986-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In fact, the current consensus among scholars is that Jericho was unoccupied from the late 15th century until the 10th/9th centuries BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although this has been questioned by recent excavations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENigro2020202–204_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENigro2020202–204-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Iron_Age">Iron Age</h3></div>
<p>Tell es-Sultan remained unoccupied from the end of the 15th to the 10th–9th centuries BCE, when the city was rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Of this new city not much more remains than a <a href="/wiki/Four-room_house" title="Four-room house">four-room house</a> on the eastern slope.<sup id="cite_ref-Negev_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Negev-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the 7th century, Jericho had become an extensive town, but this settlement was destroyed in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(587_BC)#Surrounding_areas" title="Siege of Jerusalem (587 BC)">Babylonian conquest</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">Judah</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Judah%27s_revolts_against_Babylon" title="Judah&#39;s revolts against Babylon">late 6th century</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Persian_and_Early_Hellenistic_periods">Persian and Early Hellenistic periods</h3></div>
<p>After the destruction of the Judahite city by the Babylonians in the late 6th century,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> whatever was rebuilt in the Persian period as part of the <a href="/wiki/Return_to_Zion#Return_to_Zion" title="Return to Zion">Restoration</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_captivity" title="Babylonian captivity">Babylonian captivity</a>, left only very few remains.<sup id="cite_ref-Negev_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Negev-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The tell was abandoned as a place of settlement not long after this period.<sup id="cite_ref-Negev_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Negev-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the Persian through Hellenistic periods, there is little in terms of occupation attested throughout the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Jericho went from being an administrative centre of <a href="/wiki/Yehud_Medinata" title="Yehud Medinata">Yehud Medinata</a> ("the Province of Judah") under <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Phoenicia" class="mw-redirect" title="Achaemenid Phoenicia">Persian rule</a> to serving as the private estate of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> between 336 and 323&#160;BCE after his conquest of the region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In the middle of the 2nd century BCE Jericho was under <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a> rule of the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/Syrian" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian">Syrian</a> General <a href="/wiki/Bacchides_(general)" title="Bacchides (general)">Bacchides</a> built a number of forts to strengthen the defences of the area around Jericho against the revolt by the <a href="/wiki/Macabees" class="mw-redirect" title="Macabees">Macabees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One of these forts, built at the entrance to <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Qelt" title="Wadi Qelt">Wadi Qelt</a>, was later refortified by <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">Herod the Great</a>, who named it <i>Kypros</i> after his mother.<sup id="cite_ref-Murphyp289_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphyp289-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hasmonean_and_Herodian_periods">Hasmonean and Herodian periods</h3></div>
<p>After the abandonment of the Tell es-Sultan location, the new Jericho of the Late Hellenistic or <a href="/wiki/Hasmoneans" class="mw-redirect" title="Hasmoneans">Hasmonean</a> and Early Roman or Herodian periods was established as a garden city in the vicinity of the royal estate at <a href="/wiki/Tulul_Abu_el-%27Alayiq" class="mw-redirect" title="Tulul Abu el-&#39;Alayiq">Tulul Abu el-'Alayiq</a> and expanded greatly thanks to the intensive exploitation of the springs of the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Negev_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Negev-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The new site consists of a group of low mounds on both banks of <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Qelt" title="Wadi Qelt">Wadi Qelt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobs2000691-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Hasmoneans were a dynasty descending from a priestly group (<a href="/wiki/Kohen" title="Kohen">kohanim</a>) from the <a href="/wiki/Tribe_of_Levi" title="Tribe of Levi">tribe of Levi</a>, who ruled over Judea following the success of the <a href="/wiki/Maccabean_Revolt" title="Maccabean Revolt">Maccabean Revolt</a> until Roman influence over the region brought Herod to claim the Hasmonean throne.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The rock-cut tombs of a Herodian- and Hasmonean-era cemetery lie in the lowest part of the cliffs between Nuseib al-Aweishireh and <a href="/wiki/Mount_of_Temptation" title="Mount of Temptation">Mount of Temptation</a>. They date between 100&#160;BCE and 68&#160;CE.<sup id="cite_ref-Murphyp289_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphyp289-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Herodian_period">Herodian period</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerycho50.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jerycho50.jpg/220px-Jerycho50.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jerycho50.jpg/330px-Jerycho50.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jerycho50.jpg/440px-Jerycho50.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a><figcaption>Remains from <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">Herod</a>'s palace</figcaption></figure>
<p>Herod had to lease back the royal estate at Jericho from <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra" title="Cleopatra">Cleopatra</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">Mark Antony</a> had given it to her as a gift. After their joint suicide in 30&#160;BCE, <a href="/wiki/Octavian" class="mw-redirect" title="Octavian">Octavian</a> assumed control of the Roman Empire and granted Herod absolute rule over Jericho, as part of the new <a href="/wiki/Herodian_dynasty" title="Herodian dynasty"> Herodian</a> domain. Herod's rule oversaw the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Hippodrome" title="Hippodrome">hippodrome</a>-theatre (<i>Tell es-Samrat</i>) to entertain his guests and new <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(water_supply)" title="Aqueduct (water supply)"> aqueducts</a> to irrigate the area below the cliffs and reach his winter palaces built at the site of <i>Tulul Abu el-Alaiq</i> (also written <i>ʾAlayiq</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Murphyp289_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphyp289-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Exploration_Society" title="Israel Exploration Society">Israel Exploration Society</a> published an illustrated volume of Herod's third Jericho palace.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The murder of <a href="/wiki/Aristobulus_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Aristobulus III">Aristobulus III</a> in a swimming pool at the <a href="/wiki/Hasmonean_royal_winter_palaces" class="mw-redirect" title="Hasmonean royal winter palaces">Hasmonean royal winter palaces</a>, as described by the Roman Jewish historian <a href="/wiki/Josephus" title="Josephus">Josephus</a>, took place during a banquet organized by Herod's Hasmonean mother-in-law. After the construction of the palaces, the city had functioned not only as an agricultural center and as a crossroad, but also as a winter resort for <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>'s aristocracy.<sup id="cite_ref-STF_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STF-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Herod was succeeded in <a href="/wiki/Herodian_Tetrarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Herodian Tetrarchy">Judea</a> by his son, <a href="/wiki/Herod_Archelaus" title="Herod Archelaus">Herod Archelaus</a>, who built a village in his name not far to the north, <a href="/wiki/Archela%C3%AFs" class="mw-redirect" title="Archelaïs">Archelaïs</a> (modern Khirbet al-Beiyudat), to house workers for his date plantation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>First-century Jericho is described in <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a>'s <i>Geography</i> as follows:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Jericho is a plain surrounded by a kind of mountainous country, which in a way, slopes toward it like a theatre. Here is the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(plant)" title="Phoenix (plant)">Phoenicon</a>, which is mixed also with all kinds of cultivated and fruitful trees, though it consists mostly of palm trees. It is 100 <a href="/wiki/Stadion_(unit)" title="Stadion (unit)">stadia</a> in length and is everywhere watered with streams. Here also are the Palace and the Balsam Park.<sup id="cite_ref-Murphyp289_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphyp289-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="In_the_New_Testament">In the New Testament</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Greco_-_Christ_Healing_the_Blind_-_WGA10420.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/El_Greco_-_Christ_Healing_the_Blind_-_WGA10420.jpg/220px-El_Greco_-_Christ_Healing_the_Blind_-_WGA10420.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/El_Greco_-_Christ_Healing_the_Blind_-_WGA10420.jpg/330px-El_Greco_-_Christ_Healing_the_Blind_-_WGA10420.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/El_Greco_-_Christ_Healing_the_Blind_-_WGA10420.jpg/440px-El_Greco_-_Christ_Healing_the_Blind_-_WGA10420.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="588" /></a><figcaption><i>Christ Healing the Blind in Jericho</i>, El Greco</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Christian <a href="/wiki/Gospels" class="mw-redirect" title="Gospels">Gospels</a> state that <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> of Nazareth passed through Jericho where he healed blind beggars (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Matthew%2020:29&amp;version=nrsv">Matthew 20:29</a>), and inspired a local chief <a href="/wiki/Tax_collector" title="Tax collector">tax collector</a> named <a href="/wiki/Zacchaeus" title="Zacchaeus">Zacchaeus</a> to <a href="/wiki/Repent" class="mw-redirect" title="Repent">repent</a> of his dishonest practices (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Luke%2019:1–10&amp;version=nrsv">Luke 19:1–10</a>). The road between Jerusalem and Jericho is the setting for the <a href="/wiki/Parable_of_the_Good_Samaritan" title="Parable of the Good Samaritan">Parable of the Good Samaritan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a>, in his New Testament Notes on this section of <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Luke" title="Gospel of Luke">Luke's Gospel</a>, claimed that "about twelve thousand <a href="/wiki/Kohen" title="Kohen">priests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Levite" title="Levite">Levites</a> dwelt there, who all attended the service of the <a href="/wiki/Temple_in_Jerusalem" title="Temple in Jerusalem">temple</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/William_Smith_(lexicographer)" title="William Smith (lexicographer)">Smith</a>'s <i>Bible Names Dictionary</i> suggests that "Jericho was once more 'a city of palms' when our Lord visited it. Here he restored sight to the blind (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Matthew%2020:30&amp;version=nrsv">Matthew 20:30</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Mark%2010:46&amp;version=nrsv">Mark 10:46</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Luke%2018:35&amp;version=nrsv">Luke 18:35</a>). Here the descendant of <a href="/wiki/Rahab" title="Rahab">Rahab</a> did not disdain the hospitality of Zacchaeus the <a href="/wiki/Publican" title="Publican">publican</a>. Finally, between Jerusalem and Jericho was laid the scene of his story of the good Samaritan."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Roman_province">Roman province</h3></div>
<p>After the fall of Jerusalem to Vespasian's armies in the Great Revolt of Judea in 70&#160;CE, Jericho declined rapidly, and by 100&#160;CE it was but a small Roman garrison town.<sup id="cite_ref-Loschp117_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loschp117-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A fort was built there in 130 and played a role in putting down the <a href="/wiki/Bar_Kochba_revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Bar Kochba revolt">Bar Kochba revolt</a> in 133.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Byzantine_period">Byzantine period</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_synagogues_in_the_Palestine_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient synagogues in the Palestine region">Ancient synagogues in the Palestine region</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_15003_Jericho_synagogue_mosaic.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/PikiWiki_Israel_15003_Jericho_synagogue_mosaic.JPG/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_15003_Jericho_synagogue_mosaic.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/PikiWiki_Israel_15003_Jericho_synagogue_mosaic.JPG/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_15003_Jericho_synagogue_mosaic.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/PikiWiki_Israel_15003_Jericho_synagogue_mosaic.JPG/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_15003_Jericho_synagogue_mosaic.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>Copy of Mosaic of the Shalom Al Yisrael Synagogue, 6th–7th century CE</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Itinerarium_Burdigalense" title="Itinerarium Burdigalense">Accounts</a> of Jericho by a Christian <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim">pilgrim</a> are given in 333. Shortly thereafter the built-up area of the town was abandoned and a <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> Jericho, <i>Ericha</i>, was built 1600 metres (1&#160;mi) to the east, on which the modern town is centered.<sup id="cite_ref-Loschp117_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loschp117-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> took hold in the city during the Byzantine era and the area was heavily populated. A number of monasteries and churches were built, including the <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_Saint_George_of_Choziba" title="Monastery of Saint George of Choziba">Monastery of Saint George of Choziba</a> in 340&#160;CE and a domed church dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Elisha" title="Elisha">Saint Eliseus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-STF_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STF-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At least two <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a> were also built in the 6th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-Murphyp289_55-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphyp289-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The monasteries were abandoned after the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_conquest_of_Jerusalem" title="Sasanian conquest of Jerusalem">Sasanian invasion of 614</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Jericho_synagogue" title="Jericho synagogue">Jericho synagogue</a> in the Royal Maccabean winter palace at Jericho dates from 70 to 50&#160;BCE. A synagogue dating to the late 6th or early 7th century CE was discovered in Jericho in 1936, and was named Shalom Al Yisrael Synagogue, or "peace unto Israel", after the central <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a> motto in its mosaic floor. It was controlled by Israel after the Six Day War, but after the handover to Palestinian Authority control per the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>, it has been a source of conflict. On the night of 12 October 2000, the synagogue was vandalized by Palestinians who burned holy books and relics and damaged the mosaic.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jewishjericho_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewishjericho-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Naaran" title="Naaran">Na'aran</a> synagogue, another Byzantine era construction, was discovered on the northern outskirts of Jericho in 1918. While less is known of it than Shalom Al Yisrael, it has a larger mosaic and is in similar condition.<sup id="cite_ref-jewishjericho_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewishjericho-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_Muslim_period">Early Muslim period</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Arabischer_Mosaizist_um_735_001.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Arabischer_Mosaizist_um_735_001.jpg/220px-Arabischer_Mosaizist_um_735_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Arabischer_Mosaizist_um_735_001.jpg/330px-Arabischer_Mosaizist_um_735_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Arabischer_Mosaizist_um_735_001.jpg/440px-Arabischer_Mosaizist_um_735_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2024" data-file-height="1532" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arabic</a> <a href="/wiki/Umayyad" class="mw-redirect" title="Umayyad">Umayyad</a> <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaic</a> from <a href="/wiki/Hisham%27s_Palace" title="Hisham&#39;s Palace">Hisham's Palace</a> in Jericho</figcaption></figure>
<p>Jericho, by then named "Ariha" in Arabic variation, became part of <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">Jund Filastin</a> ("Military District of Palestine"), part of the larger province of <a href="/wiki/Bilad_al-Sham" title="Bilad al-Sham">Bilad al-Sham</a>. The Arab Muslim historian Musa b. 'Uqba (died 758) recorded that <a href="/wiki/Caliph" class="mw-redirect" title="Caliph">caliph</a> <a href="/wiki/Umar_ibn_al-Khattab" class="mw-redirect" title="Umar ibn al-Khattab">Umar ibn al-Khattab</a> exiled the Jews and Christians of <a href="/wiki/Khaybar" title="Khaybar">Khaybar</a> to Jericho (and Tayma).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>By 659, that district had come under the control of <a href="/wiki/Mu%27awiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Mu&#39;awiya">Mu'awiya</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad dynasty</a>. That year, an earthquake destroyed Jericho.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A decade later, the pilgrim <a href="/wiki/Arculf" title="Arculf">Arculf</a> visited Jericho and found it in ruins, all its "miserable Canaanite" inhabitants now dispersed in shanty towns around the Dead Sea shore.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A palatial complex long attributed to the tenth Umayyad caliph, <a href="/wiki/Hisham_ibn_Abd_al-Malik" title="Hisham ibn Abd al-Malik">Hisham ibn Abd al-Malik</a> (r. 724–743) and thus known as <a href="/wiki/Hisham%27s_Palace" title="Hisham&#39;s Palace">Hisham's Palace</a>, is located at Khirbet al-Mafjar, about 1.5 kilometres (1&#160;mi) north of Tell es-Sultan. This <a href="/wiki/Desert_castle" class="mw-redirect" title="Desert castle">"desert castle" or <i>qasr</i></a> was more likely built by Caliph <a href="/wiki/Al-Walid_II" title="Al-Walid II">Walid ibn Yazid</a> (r. 743–744), who was assassinated before he could complete the construction.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The remains of two mosques, a courtyard, mosaics, and other items can still be seen <i>in situ</i> today. The unfinished structure was largely destroyed in an earthquake in 747.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Umayyad rule ended in 750 and was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> caliphates of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbasid">Abbasid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fatimid" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimid">Fatimid</a> dynasties. Irrigated agriculture was developed under Islamic rule, reaffirming Jericho's reputation as a fertile "City of the Palms".<sup id="cite_ref-Shahinp285_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shahinp285-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al-Muqaddasi" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Muqaddasi">Al-Maqdisi</a>, the Arab geographer, wrote in 985 that "the water of Jericho is held to be the highest and best in all <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">Bananas</a> are plentiful, also <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_dactylifera" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenix dactylifera">dates</a> and flowers of fragrant odor".<sup id="cite_ref-Shahinp283_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shahinp283-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Jericho is also referred to by him as one of the principal cities of Jund Filastin.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Crusader_period">Crusader period</h3></div>
<p>In 1179, the Crusaders rebuilt the Monastery of St. George of Koziba, at its original site 10 kilometres (6&#160;mi) from the center of town.
