They also built another two churches and a monastery dedicated to <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Baptist</a>, and were credited by 19th-century authors with introducing <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> production to the city,<sup id="cite_ref-Hull_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hull-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although now scholars date it to the pre-Crusader, Early Arab period. The Crusaders, however, have raised sugar production to the level of a large-scale industry. The site of Tawahin es-Sukkar (lit. "sugar mills") holds remains of a Crusader sugar production facility. In 1187, the Crusaders were evicted by the <a href="/wiki/Ayyubid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayyubid">Ayyubid</a> forces of <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Saladin</a> after their victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hattin" title="Battle of Hattin">Battle of Hattin</a>, and the town slowly went into decline.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ayyubid_and_Mamluk_periods">Ayyubid and Mamluk periods</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_chronicles_f_50r_1.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Nuremberg_chronicles_f_50r_1.png/220px-Nuremberg_chronicles_f_50r_1.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Nuremberg_chronicles_f_50r_1.png/330px-Nuremberg_chronicles_f_50r_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Nuremberg_chronicles_f_50r_1.png/440px-Nuremberg_chronicles_f_50r_1.png 2x" data-file-width="883" data-file-height="536" /></a><figcaption>Jericho, as depicted in the 1493 <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Chronicle" title="Nuremberg Chronicle">Nuremberg Chronicle</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1226, Arab geographer <a href="/wiki/Yaqut_al-Hamawi" title="Yaqut al-Hamawi">Yaqut al-Hamawi</a> said of Jericho, "it has many palm trees, also sugarcane in quantities, and bananas. The best of all the sugar in the <i><a href="/wiki/Jordan_Valley" title="Jordan Valley">Ghaur</a></i> land is made here." In the 14th century, <a href="/wiki/Abu_al-Fida" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu al-Fida">Abu al-Fida</a> writes there are <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a> mines in Jericho, "the only ones in Palestine".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ottoman_period">Ottoman period</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerico1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Jerico1.jpg/220px-Jerico1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Jerico1.jpg/330px-Jerico1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Jerico1.jpg/440px-Jerico1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1084" data-file-height="700" /></a><figcaption>Postcard image depicting Jericho in the late 19th or early 20th century</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="16th_century">16th century</h4></div>
<p>Jericho was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1517 with all of <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>, and in 1545 a revenue of 19,000 <a href="/wiki/Ak%C3%A7e" title="Akçe">Akçe</a> was recorded, destined for the new <a href="/wiki/Waqf" title="Waqf">Waqf</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Haseki_Sultan_Imaret" title="Haseki Sultan Imaret">Haseki Sultan Imaret</a> of Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-Singerp52_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singerp52-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The villagers processed <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a> as one source of revenue, using a cauldron specifically for this purpose that was loaned to them by the Ottoman authorities in Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-Singerp120_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singerp120-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later that century, the Jericho revenues no longer went to the Haseki Sultan Imaret.<sup id="cite_ref-Singerp126_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singerp126-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1596 Jericho appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Daftar" class="mw-redirect" title="Daftar">tax registers</a> under the name of <i>Riha</i>, being in the <i><a href="/wiki/Nahiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahiya">nahiya</a></i> of Al-Quds in the <i><a href="/wiki/Liwa_(Arabic)" title="Liwa (Arabic)">liwa</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Al-Quds" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Quds">Al-Quds</a>. It had a population of 51 households, all <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>. They paid a fixed tax-rate of 33.3% on agricultural products, including wheat, barley, summer crops, vineyards and fruit trees, goats and beehives, water buffaloes, in addition to occasional revenues; a total of 40,000 <a href="/wiki/Ak%C3%A7e" title="Akçe">Akçe</a>. All of the revenue still went to a Waqf.<sup id="cite_ref-HA114_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HA114-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="17th_century">17th century</h4></div>
<p>The French traveller <a href="/wiki/Laurent_d%27Arvieux" title="Laurent d&#39;Arvieux">Laurent d'Arvieux</a> described the city in 1659 as "now desolate, and consists only of about fifty poor houses, in bad condition ... The plain around is extremely fertile; the soil is middling fat; but it is watered by several rivulets, which flow into the Jordan. Notwithstanding these advantages only the gardens adjacent to the town are cultivated."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="19th_century">19th century</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_aquaduct_near_Jericho.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roman_aquaduct_near_Jericho.jpg/220px-Roman_aquaduct_near_Jericho.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roman_aquaduct_near_Jericho.jpg/330px-Roman_aquaduct_near_Jericho.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roman_aquaduct_near_Jericho.jpg/440px-Roman_aquaduct_near_Jericho.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2409" data-file-height="1626" /></a><figcaption>Roman aqueducts</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the 19th century, European scholars, archaeologists and missionaries visited often.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the time it was an oasis in a poor state, similar to other regions in the plains and deserts.<sup id="cite_ref-benarieh_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-benarieh-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Robinson_(scholar)" title="Edward Robinson (scholar)">Edward Robinson</a> (1838) reported 50 families, which were about 200 people,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Titus_Tobler" title="Titus Tobler">Titus Tobler</a> (1854) reported some 30 poor huts, whose residents paid a total of 3611 <a href="/wiki/Kuru%C5%9F" title="Kuruş">kuruş</a> in tax.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Abraham Samuel Herschberg (1858–1943) also reported after his 1899–1900 travels in the region<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> of some 30 poor huts and 300 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At that time, Jericho was the residence of the region's Turkish governor. The main water sources for the village were a spring called <i>Ein al-Sultan</i>, lit. "Sultan's Spring", in Arabic and <i>Ein Elisha</i>, lit. "Elisha Spring", in Hebrew, and springs in <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Qelt" title="Wadi Qelt">Wadi Qelt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-benarieh_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-benarieh-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/James_Silk_Buckingham" title="James Silk Buckingham">J. S. Buckingham</a> (1786–1855) describes in his 1822 book how the male villagers of er-Riha, although nominally sedentary, engaged in <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a>-style <a href="/wiki/Raid_(military)#Bedouin_&#39;&#39;ghazzu&#39;&#39;" title="Raid (military)">raiding, or <i>ghazzu</i></a>: the little land cultivation he observed was done by women and children, while men spent most of their time riding through the plains and engaging in "robbery and plunder", their main and most profitable activity.<sup id="cite_ref-Tribal_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tribal-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> village list from around 1870 showed that <i>Riha</i>, Jericho, had 36 houses and a population of 105, though the population count included men only.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/Excavation_(archaeology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Excavation (archaeology)">excavation</a> at Tell es-Sultan was carried out in 1867.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="20th_century">20th century</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%94%D7%9C_%D7%9C%D7%A6%D7%93_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%94%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%93%D7%9F_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95-JNF022256.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%94%D7%9C_%D7%9C%D7%A6%D7%93_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%94%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%93%D7%9F_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95-JNF022256.jpeg/220px-%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%94%D7%9C_%D7%9C%D7%A6%D7%93_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%94%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%93%D7%9F_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95-JNF022256.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="223" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%94%D7%9C_%D7%9C%D7%A6%D7%93_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%94%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%93%D7%9F_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95-JNF022256.jpeg/330px-%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%94%D7%9C_%D7%9C%D7%A6%D7%93_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%94%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%93%D7%9F_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95-JNF022256.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%94%D7%9C_%D7%9C%D7%A6%D7%93_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%94%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%93%D7%9F_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95-JNF022256.jpeg/440px-%D7%9E%D7%90%D7%94%D7%9C_%D7%9C%D7%A6%D7%93_%D7%9E%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9F_%D7%94%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%93%D7%9F_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95-JNF022256.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="567" data-file-height="576" /></a><figcaption>Jericho, the Jordan Hotel, 1912</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_views_of_Palestine._Air_route_following_the_old_Jerusalem-Jericho_Road._Modern_Jericho._Taken_above_the_Ain_Sultan_road_looking_S._LOC_matpc.22116.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Air_views_of_Palestine._Air_route_following_the_old_Jerusalem-Jericho_Road._Modern_Jericho._Taken_above_the_Ain_Sultan_road_looking_S._LOC_matpc.22116.jpg/220px-Air_views_of_Palestine._Air_route_following_the_old_Jerusalem-Jericho_Road._Modern_Jericho._Taken_above_the_Ain_Sultan_road_looking_S._LOC_matpc.22116.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Air_views_of_Palestine._Air_route_following_the_old_Jerusalem-Jericho_Road._Modern_Jericho._Taken_above_the_Ain_Sultan_road_looking_S._LOC_matpc.22116.jpg/330px-Air_views_of_Palestine._Air_route_following_the_old_Jerusalem-Jericho_Road._Modern_Jericho._Taken_above_the_Ain_Sultan_road_looking_S._LOC_matpc.22116.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Air_views_of_Palestine._Air_route_following_the_old_Jerusalem-Jericho_Road._Modern_Jericho._Taken_above_the_Ain_Sultan_road_looking_S._LOC_matpc.22116.jpg/440px-Air_views_of_Palestine._Air_route_following_the_old_Jerusalem-Jericho_Road._Modern_Jericho._Taken_above_the_Ain_Sultan_road_looking_S._LOC_matpc.22116.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4376" data-file-height="2916" /></a><figcaption>Jericho from the air in 1931</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Jerusalem" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Church of Jerusalem">Greek Orthodox</a> monasteries of <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_St._George_of_Choziba" class="mw-redirect" title="Monastery of St. George of Choziba">St. George of Choziba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qasr_el_Yahud" class="mw-redirect" title="Qasr el Yahud">John the Baptist</a> were refounded and completed in 1901 and 1904, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="British_Mandate_period">British Mandate period</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:AN_AERIAL_PHOTO_OF_JERICHO._%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%90%D7%95%D7%99%D7%A8_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.D332-058.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/AN_AERIAL_PHOTO_OF_JERICHO._%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%90%D7%95%D7%99%D7%A8_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.D332-058.jpg/220px-AN_AERIAL_PHOTO_OF_JERICHO._%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%90%D7%95%D7%99%D7%A8_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.D332-058.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/AN_AERIAL_PHOTO_OF_JERICHO._%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%90%D7%95%D7%99%D7%A8_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.D332-058.jpg/330px-AN_AERIAL_PHOTO_OF_JERICHO._%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%90%D7%95%D7%99%D7%A8_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.D332-058.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/AN_AERIAL_PHOTO_OF_JERICHO._%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%90%D7%95%D7%99%D7%A8_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.D332-058.jpg/440px-AN_AERIAL_PHOTO_OF_JERICHO._%D7%A6%D7%99%D7%9C%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%90%D7%95%D7%99%D7%A8_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.D332-058.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="2048" /></a><figcaption>Jericho 1938</figcaption></figure>
<p>After the collapse of the Ottoman Empire at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Jericho came under British rule, as part of <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a>.
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/1922_census_of_Palestine" title="1922 census of Palestine">1922 census of Palestine</a>, Jericho had 1,029 inhabitants (931 Muslims, 92 Christians, and six Jews).<sup id="cite_ref-Census1922a_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census1922a-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Christian population consisted of 45 Orthodox, 12 Roman Catholics, 13 Greek Catholics (<a href="/wiki/Melkite_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Catholics">Melkite Catholics</a>), 6 Syrian Catholic, 11 Armenians, four Copts and one Church of England.<sup id="cite_ref-Census1922b_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census1922b-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1927, an <a href="/wiki/1927_Jericho_earthquake" title="1927 Jericho earthquake">earthquake struck</a> and affected Jericho and other cities. Around 300 people died,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but by the <a href="/wiki/1931_census_of_Palestine" title="1931 census of Palestine">1931 census</a> the population had increased to 1,693 inhabitants (1,512 Muslims, 170 Christians, seven Druze, and four Jews), in 347 houses.<sup id="cite_ref-Census31_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census31-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1938 statistics, Jericho lists a population of 1,996 people (including five Jews).<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Village_Statistics,_1945" title="Village Statistics, 1945">1945 statistics</a>, Jericho's population was 3,010 (2,570 Muslims, 260 Christians, 170 Jews, and 10 "other"<sup id="cite_ref-1945p24_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1945p24-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) and it had jurisdiction over 37,481 <a href="/wiki/Dunam" title="Dunam">dunams</a> of land.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Of this, 948 dunams were used for citrus and bananas, 5,873 dunams were for plantations and irrigable land, 9,141 for cereals,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while a total of 38 dunams were urban, built-up areas.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> The British built fortresses in Jericho with the help of the Jewish company <a href="/wiki/Solel_Boneh" title="Solel Boneh">Solel Boneh</a>, and bridges were rigged with explosives in preparation for a possible invasion by German allied forces.<sup id="cite_ref-Frilingp65_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frilingp65-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Jordanian_period">Jordanian period</h3></div>
<p>Jericho came under <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordanian</a> control after the <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab–Israeli War">1948 Arab–Israeli War</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Jericho_Conference" title="Jericho Conference">Jericho Conference</a>, organized by King Abdullah and attended by over 2,000 Palestinian delegates in 1948 proclaimed "His Majesty Abdullah as King of all Palestine" and called for "the unification of Palestine and Transjordan as a step toward full <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> unity". In mid-1950, Jordan formally annexed the West Bank and Jericho residents, like other residents of West Bank localities became Jordanian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-Benvenistip27_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benvenistip27-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1961, the population of Jericho was 10,166,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> of whom 935 were Christian, and the rest were Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1967_and_aftermath">1967 and aftermath</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_OCHA_OpT_map_Jericho.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/2018_OCHA_OpT_map_Jericho.jpg/290px-2018_OCHA_OpT_map_Jericho.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="410" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/2018_OCHA_OpT_map_Jericho.jpg/435px-2018_OCHA_OpT_map_Jericho.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/2018_OCHA_OpT_map_Jericho.jpg/580px-2018_OCHA_OpT_map_Jericho.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1768" data-file-height="2500" /></a><figcaption>2018 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs" title="United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs">United Nations</a> map of the area, showing the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Israeli occupation of the West Bank">Israeli occupation</a> arrangements</figcaption></figure>
<p>Jericho has been <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">occupied</a> by <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> of 1967 along with the rest of the West Bank. It was the first city handed over to <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> control in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CSM_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSM-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The limited Palestinian self-rule of Jericho was agreed on in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Jericho_Agreement" title="Gaza–Jericho Agreement">Gaza–Jericho Agreement</a> of 4 May 1994. Part of the agreement was a "Protocol on Economic Relations", signed on 29 April 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city is in an enclave of the Jordan Valley that is in <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_enclaves" title="Palestinian enclaves">Area A</a> of the West Bank, while the surrounding area is designated as being in Area C under full Israeli military control. Four roadblocks encircle the enclave, restricting Jericho's Palestinian population's movement through the West Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In response to the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Second_Intifada" title="Second Intifada">Second Intifada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suicide_bombings" class="mw-redirect" title="Suicide bombings">suicide bombings</a>, Jericho was re-occupied by Israeli troops.<sup id="cite_ref-CSM_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSM-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2-metre (6&#160;ft 7&#160;in) deep trench was built around a large part of the city to control Palestinian traffic to and from Jericho.<sup id="cite_ref-ARIJ_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARIJ-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 March 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> launched <a href="/wiki/Operation_Bringing_Home_the_Goods" title="Operation Bringing Home the Goods">Operation Bringing Home the Goods</a>, raiding a Jericho prison to capture the PFLP general secretary, <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Sa%27adat" title="Ahmad Sa&#39;adat">Ahmad Sa'adat</a>, and five other prisoners, all of whom had been charged with assassinating the Israeli tourist minister <a href="/wiki/Rehavam_Zeevi" class="mw-redirect" title="Rehavam Zeevi">Rehavam Zeevi</a> in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After Hamas assaulted a neighborhood in Gaza mostly populated by the Fatah-aligned <a href="/wiki/Hilles_clan" title="Hilles clan">Hilles clan</a>, in response to their attack that killed six Hamas members, the Hilles clan was relocated to Jericho on 4 August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, Palestinian Authority Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Salam_Fayyad" title="Salam Fayyad">Salam Fayyad</a> and U.S. <a href="/wiki/Assistant_Secretary_of_State_for_International_Narcotics_and_Law_Enforcement_Affairs" title="Assistant Secretary of State for International Narcotics and Law Enforcement Affairs">Assistant Secretary of State for International Narcotics and Law Enforcement Affairs</a> David Johnson inaugurated the Presidential Guard Training Center in Jericho, a $9.1&#160;million training facility for <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Security_Forces" title="Palestinian National Security Forces">Palestinian Authority security forces</a> built with U.S. funding.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2024, a Jericho street was named after <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Bushnell" class="mw-redirect" title="Aaron Bushnell">Aaron Bushnell</a>, a U.S. soldier who self-immolated in support of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography_and_environment">Geography and environment</h2></div>
<p>Jericho is located 258 metres (846&#160;ft) below <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oasis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Qelt" title="Wadi Qelt">Wadi Qelt</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Valley_(Middle_East)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jordan Valley (Middle East)">Jordan Valley</a>, which makes it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_elevation" title="List of cities by elevation">lowest city in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Murphyp288_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murphyp288-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Holmanp1391_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmanp1391-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The nearby spring of <i>Ein es-Sultan</i> produces 3.8&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (1,000 gallons) of water per minute, irrigating some 10 square kilometres (2,500 acres) through multiple channels and feeding into the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_River" title="Jordan River">Jordan River</a>, 10 kilometres (6&#160;mi) away.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringp367_20-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringp367-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Holmanp1391_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmanp1391-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1208px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Jericho_Panorama.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Panorama of Jericho"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Jericho_Panorama.jpg/1200px-Jericho_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1200" height="258" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Jericho_Panorama.jpg/1800px-Jericho_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Jericho_Panorama.jpg/2400px-Jericho_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6499" data-file-height="1397" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jericho_Panorama.jpg" title="File:Jericho Panorama.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of Jericho</div></div></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Important_Bird_Area">Important Bird Area</h3></div>
<p>A 3,500&#160;ha (8,600-acre) site encompassing the city of Jericho and its immediate surrounds has been recognised as an <a href="/wiki/Important_Bird_Area" title="Important Bird Area">Important Bird Area</a> (IBA) by <a href="/wiki/BirdLife_International" title="BirdLife International">BirdLife International</a> because it supports populations of <a href="/wiki/Black_francolin" title="Black francolin">black francolins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanner_falcon" title="Lanner falcon">lanner falcons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesser_kestrel" title="Lesser kestrel">lesser kestrels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dead_Sea_sparrow" title="Dead Sea sparrow">Dead Sea sparrows</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bli_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bli-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3></div>
<p>Annual rainfall is 204&#160;mm (8.0&#160;in), mostly concentrated in the winter months and into early spring.<sup id="cite_ref-NS_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NS-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The average temperature is 11&#160;°C (52&#160;°F) in January and 31&#160;°C (88&#160;°F) in July. According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, Jericho has a <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a> (<i>BWh</i>). Rich alluvial soil and abundant spring water have made Jericho an attractive place for settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmanp1391_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmanp1391-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_1536_Jericho_municipality_%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%99%D7%AA_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/PikiWiki_Israel_1536_Jericho_municipality_%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%99%D7%AA_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_1536_Jericho_municipality_%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%99%D7%AA_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/PikiWiki_Israel_1536_Jericho_municipality_%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%99%D7%AA_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_1536_Jericho_municipality_%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%99%D7%AA_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/PikiWiki_Israel_1536_Jericho_municipality_%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%99%D7%AA_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_1536_Jericho_municipality_%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%99%D7%AA_%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1247" data-file-height="863" /></a><figcaption>Municipality of Jericho, 1967</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the first census carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Central_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Palestinian Central Bureau of Statistics">Palestinian Central Bureau of Statistics</a> (PCBS), in 1997, Jericho's population was 14,674. <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugee" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian refugee">Palestinian refugees</a> constituted a significant 43.6% of the residents or 6,393 people.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The gender make-up of the city was 51% male and 49% female. Jericho has a young population, with nearly half (49.2%) of the inhabitants being under the age of 20. People between the ages of 20 and 44 made up 36.2% of the population, 10.7% between the ages of 45 and 64, and 3.6% were over the age of 64.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the 2007 census by the PCBS, Jericho had a population of 18,346.<sup id="cite_ref-PCBS_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCBS-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Demographics have varied widely depending on the dominant ethnic group and rule in the region over the past three thousand years. In a 1945 land and population survey by <a href="/wiki/Sami_Hadawi" title="Sami Hadawi">Sami Hadawi</a>, 3,010 inhabitants is the figure given for Jericho, of which 94% (2840) were Arab and 6% (170) were Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today, the overwhelming majority of the population is <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Christians" title="Palestinian Christians">Christian</a> community makes up around 1% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-sussi_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sussi-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A large community of <a href="/wiki/Black_Palestinians" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Palestinians">black Palestinians</a> is present in Jericho.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_1539_The_market_of_Jericho_%D7%94%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%A7_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/PikiWiki_Israel_1539_The_market_of_Jericho_%D7%94%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%A7_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_1539_The_market_of_Jericho_%D7%94%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%A7_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/PikiWiki_Israel_1539_The_market_of_Jericho_%D7%94%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%A7_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_1539_The_market_of_Jericho_%D7%94%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%A7_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/PikiWiki_Israel_1539_The_market_of_Jericho_%D7%94%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%A7_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_1539_The_market_of_Jericho_%D7%94%D7%A9%D7%95%D7%A7_%D7%91%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%97%D7%95.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1221" data-file-height="860" /></a><figcaption>Jericho marketplace, 1967</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1994, Israel and Palestine signed an economic accord that enabled Palestinians in Jericho to open banks, collect taxes and engage in export and import in preparation for self-rule.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
Agriculture is another source of income, with banana groves ringing the city.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Jericho Agro-Industrial Park is a public-private enterprise being developed in the Jericho area. Agricultural processing companies are being offered financial concessions to lease plots of land in the park in a bid to boost Jericho's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerycho9.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Jerycho9.jpg/220px-Jerycho9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Jerycho9.jpg/330px-Jerycho9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Jerycho9.jpg/440px-Jerycho9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a><figcaption>Jericho cable car</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1998, a $150&#160;million casino-hotel was built in Jericho with the backing of Yasser Arafat.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The casino is now closed, though the hotel on the premises is open for guests.
</p><p>In 2010, Jericho, with its proximity to the Dead Sea, was declared the most popular destination among Palestinian tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Biblical_and_Christian_landmarks">Biblical and Christian landmarks</h3></div>
<p>Christian tourism is one of Jericho's primary sources of income. There are several major Christian pilgrimage sites in and around Jericho.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ein_es-Sultan" title="Ein es-Sultan">Ein es-Sultan</a>, known as the Spring of Elisha to Jews and Christians;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Qasr_al-Yahud" title="Qasr al-Yahud">Qasr al-Yahud</a> on the Jordan River, across from <a href="/wiki/Al-Maghtas" title="Al-Maghtas">Bethany beyond the Jordan</a>, traditionally identified as the location of the <a href="/wiki/Baptism_of_Jesus" title="Baptism of Jesus">baptism of Jesus</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_of_Temptation" title="Mount of Temptation">Mount of Temptation</a> (Jebel Quruntul), traditionally identified as the location of the <a href="/wiki/Temptation_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Temptation of Jesus">Temptation of Jesus</a>;</li>
<li>The Greek Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_the_Temptation" title="Monastery of the Temptation">Monastery of the Temptation</a> halfway up the mountain, beside a cave said to be the location where Jesus fasted for 40 days. It is connected to Jericho by a cable car;<sup id="cite_ref-jpost_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2 sycamore trees separately mentioned as the one mentioned in relation to <a href="/wiki/Zacchaeus" title="Zacchaeus">Zacchaeus</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Deir_Hajla" title="Deir Hajla">Deir Hajla</a>, the monastery of <a href="/wiki/Gerasimus_of_the_Jordan" title="Gerasimus of the Jordan">St. Gerasimos</a> in the Jordan Valley near Jericho;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Monastery,_Wadi_Qelt" class="mw-redirect" title="St. George&#39;s Monastery, Wadi Qelt">Saint George Monastery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Qelt" title="Wadi Qelt">Wadi Qelt</a> above Jericho.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Archaeological_landmarks">Archaeological landmarks</h3></div>
<ul><li>Stone, Bronze and Iron Age cities at <b>Tell es-Sultan</b>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hasmonean_royal_winter_palaces" class="mw-redirect" title="Hasmonean royal winter palaces">Hasmonean and Herodian winter palaces</a> at <b>Tulul Abu el-'Alayiq</b>;</li>
<li>Byzantine-period synagogues at Jericho (<a href="/wiki/Jericho_synagogue" title="Jericho synagogue">Shalom Al Yisrael Synagogue</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Naaran" title="Naaran">Na'aran</a>;</li>
<li>Umayyad palace at Khirbet al-Mafjar known as <a href="/wiki/Hisham%27s_Palace" title="Hisham&#39;s Palace">Hisham's Palace</a>;</li>
<li>Crusader sugar production facility at <b>Tawahin es-Sukkar</b> (lit. "sugar mills");</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nabi_Musa" title="Nabi Musa">Nabi Musa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> shrine claimed to be the resting place of <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a> ("Prophet Musa" to the Muslims)</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Schools_and_religious_institutions">Schools and religious institutions</h2></div>
<p>In 1925, Christian friars opened a school for 100 pupils that became the Terra Santa School. The city has 22 state schools and a number of private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-sussi_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sussi-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Health_care">Health care</h2></div>
<p>In April 2010, the United States Agency for International Development (USAID) held a groundbreaking ceremony for the renovation of the <a href="/wiki/Jericho_Governmental_Hospital" title="Jericho Governmental Hospital">Jericho Governmental Hospital</a>. USAID is providing $2.5&#160;million in funding for this project.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Sports">Sports</h2></div>
<p>The sports team <a href="/wiki/Hilal_Areeha" title="Hilal Areeha">Hilal Areeha</a> plays <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> in the West Bank First Division. They play home games in the 15,000-spectator <a href="/wiki/Jericho_International_Stadium" title="Jericho International Stadium">Jericho International Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Twin_towns_–_sister_cities"><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities"></span>Twin towns – sister cities</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in the State of Palestine">List of twin towns and sister cities in the State of Palestine</a></div>
<p>Jericho is <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">twinned</a> with:<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Musa_Alami" title="Musa Alami">Musa Alami</a></li></ul>
